Post #1  (forum post #652937)
Author    : tk1608
Date      : Aug 19, 2008 at 2:32 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi All

I've decided to give it a go, so here's a few progress pics.

This is just the main shape cut from 1.5mm styrene.

[IMAGE: Falcon1.jpg]

A bit of this and that to give it some support.

[IMAGE: Falcon2.jpg]

More tubing and stuff added plus lights.

[IMAGE: Falcon3.jpg]

A pic to show the lights without the flash.

[IMAGE: Falcon4.jpg]

The lights are Ikea cabinet lights. I noticed a post here about them, I think it was on the ironman thread...I can't find the darn thread now..but Thanks very much to whoever that was, I had no idea these lights exhisted but for that post. I had a friend of a friend add the LEDs for the headlights to the curcuit. It needed to have the voltage reduced for the LEDs 'cos the Ikea set puts out 12v, and electronics is not my thing.

I'm gonna add one of the round set...see below..for the cockpit lights, and I have three of the striplight set installed for the engine lights. I wanted to use all four so it was really bright, but couldn't cram four in.

It needs diffusing a bit, I thought I could stick some alu foil inside to hopefully even out the light, and add a blueish tint if I can.

Round IKEA | Integrated lighting | Bookcase integrated lighting | DIODER | Multipurpose lighting

Strip IKEA | Integrated lighting | Bookcases integrated lighting | DIODER | Lighting strip

Anyway, there you go..there's a loooooong way to go yet and I'm not even sure that I will finish this. There's areas that I'm still not sure about, that I hope I can figure out when I get to them. We'll see..

Cheers

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress pics/small update

Hey all, just a couple more pics with a few ribs added...slow going but progress all the same.

[IMAGE: Ribsshrunk1.jpg]

[IMAGE: Ribsshrunk2.jpg]

I have a question about the plating cut-outs/notches that I hope someone can help with...just wondering what size they need to be ?

I have a nibbler from micro mark that cuts notches almost 1/4 of an inch wide (6mm), this seems too big to me. I think it should be more like 1/8th, or maybe 3/16ths

Anyone know ?...I hope I don't need to cut them all out by hand with a knife, I'll be at it forever..

Cheers

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress pics/small update

Hey Stu, I got the micromark one 'cos someone mentioned it here I think, but before I went for that I tried to find a supplier more local to me. My search found that Amazon of all places listed a nibbler made by Draper Tools. I dunno if you have that where you are. I didn't find out what size notch the Draper one cuts though.. I decided that the micromark was probably best to go for, but it's something to consider I suppose..

Cheers

Phil

Post #20  (forum post #685718)
Author    : BrundelFly
Date      : Oct 4, 2008 at 10:49 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress pics/small update

The Nibbler was used on the 5 footer.

Moe and I both agreed that the Nibbler cannot be used on the 32 inch.

We cut our notches by hand mostly.

I modified my nibbler so it didnt cut as deep initially. But eventually abandon that and did by hand.

Re: 32" Falcon Progress pics/another update new pics

Hi All

A bit more progress, this was my first attempt at the mandible panels, as you can see the notches are too big. This was with the standard micromark nibbler..

[IMAGE: MPsshrunk1.jpg]

Second go...looks about right now I reckon,..well, near enough..These were all cut with the trusty knife one at a time.

[IMAGE: MPsShrunk2.jpg]

Panels stuck on, love that humbrol liquid cement, the smell was nice, lost a few more brain cells..

[IMAGE: Mandiblesshrunk.jpg]

A bit of skinning...sorry about the messy workspace, I didn't realise what a disgrace it was until I saw these pics.:lol

[IMAGE: Skinshrunk2.jpg]

And a bit more..

[IMAGE: Skinshrunk3.jpg]

All the top skins are on now, start on the bottom after the weekend.

Looking forward to boxing in the docking tube walkways and those front jaw thingy areas.

Not looking forward to cutting the cockpit tunnel tho..getting the angle right and making it fit the curve of the hull might be a difficult thing.

Cheers

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/update even newer pics

Hi all

Another update..

just a bit of work on the docking corridors, card mock up

[IMAGE: small2.jpg]

Starting to build the gear bays

[IMAGE: small4.jpg]

[IMAGE: small5.jpg]

Boxing in the rear gear bay

[IMAGE: small6.jpg]

The lower jaw box with nose gear bay with edges sanded flush

[IMAGE: small8.jpg]

Top View with cockpit tube, this was difficult for me to get right to say the least. I knew it wouldn't be easy, but it was worse. I think it's ok now, at least it looks about right when I view it from the front. The walls of this tubing are really thick, it was a swine to cut. I cut too much off (wanted to avoid that) and had to re-attach some at the back.

[IMAGE: small7.jpg]

There you go, hope you likey

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/update newer pics page 4

Hey Phil, that's looking great !

I had the same issues with my cockpit tubing and with the jaw boxes, this is not an easy build at all... And all Falcon's builders get my respect ! I hope I'll be able to finish one someday lol

You're almost done with the basic shape and the fun will start with hull plating ! :love I used Tamiya extra fluid glue (the green one) to glue the plates and I had some problems several months after :s If I had to start again I would use another glue !

Anyway I wish you good luck for the rest of your build, it's very good and clean so far, it will be stunning once finished !

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/update newer pics page 6

Thanks for the kind words again guys,

Just to answer that kit part question, it's from a 1/12th tamiya ferrari, this kit..

[IMAGE: ferrari.jpg]

I can't remember the actual kit number, this kit along with the 1/12th renault that Stu mentioned, have been sitting in my Mum's garage for years gradually falling apart. I thought I'd strip 'em down and use them for this build.

I don't have the plans anymore, so I can't give the part number, but here's a close up of the remains of the part and where it goes on the side of the engine.

[IMAGE: FP2SMALL.jpg]

[IMAGE: FPsmall.jpg]

I think this engine's used on the Bwing too..

As I say, this is not an accurate part for the 32", but I just thought it looked ok so stuck it on.

I hope that helps and if it turns out to be a part not discovered yet I'd be very pleased to have found something that could be new..

Cheers

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/update newer pics page 10

Ok, so more piccys..I realised after I got some more reference and parts, that the pits I'd made were too small to fit the parts into. So I marked out a larger hole and chopped it out..

[IMAGE: newpitsml.jpg]

[IMAGE: pit2sml.jpg]

This is it almost finished, just the new walls to sand down and tidy up

[IMAGE: pitdetail1sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: pit3smlalldetail.jpg]

I think it's about right now, I added a couple of other bits just to fill space, but it'll be hidden under the plating, so there was no need really. I scratched the tam 232 bit 'cos my attempt to do a bit of casting a few weeks back went wrong. This was one of the bits I was trying to cast. It was quicker to do that than wait for the darn rubber to set etc, no patience..anyway, when it's under paint who's gonna know.:lol

This is the other side, had to make this hole bigger too, 

[IMAGE: pit5sml.jpg]

And onto the dreaded plating...:wacko

[IMAGE: pitpaintplatingsml.jpg]

I shot some primer into the holes before I started the plating, I thought it would be a bit difficult to get into there with the paint after the plates were on.

That's it for now.

Cheers

Phil

More pics..Completed pit area with chips added

[IMAGE: Blockpitlatestsml.jpg]

And the other side, a bit out of focus, but you get the idea..

[IMAGE: Shermpitlatsestsml.jpg]

This is the radar area with penciled marks to test where the plates should be, lots of measureing pics and stuff to figure this out. A bit of messing about was needed to get it to work out though, because most pictures are taken from angles that throw out the perspective.

[IMAGE: Dishsectmarkssmall.jpg]

This is how I tranfered the markings to the styrene plates..I hope you can see what I've done. I placed the straight edge of the styrene against a straight pencil line and put the curves in with the large compass.

[IMAGE: DishSectmarkstransfersml.jpg]

Bit more of the same... as the plating was added, I butted up against that to add the next plate.

[IMAGE: Dishsectalmosttransfersml.jpg]

The next pics are the progress as the plates were added.

[IMAGE: Dishsectpartialplatesml.jpg]

[IMAGE: Dishsectplatealmostdonesml.jpg]

[IMAGE: Dishsectcompletesml.jpg]

And finally to where I'm am now with chips stuck on and a bit of piping

[IMAGE: Dishsectcompletechipssml.jpg]

Until I looked closely at pics I thought the plates lined up in a sorta organised way, but they are stepped in places and have small gaps where there's no plating. I'm sure ILM did this to make copying this thing more difficult..

Anyway let me know what you think

Cheers

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #123  (forum post #1001841)
Author    : tk1608
Date      : Oct 5, 2009 at 2:03 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ even more newer pics page 12

Hey guys, anyone know what the part marked in red is from please ?

[IMAGE: sharpen2redbox.jpg]

I cut the curves in the plating by hand, just following the pencil line, or slightly to one side of the line. A bit of sanding here and there tidied up the edges and helped the fit. It was too much messing about to set up the cutter to do each individual plate. 

This is the cutter, you can get these at stationery stores, I've seen them in card shops and those places that do computers and office stuff. It'll cut circles up to 12 inches diameter.

[IMAGE: cuttersml.jpg]

This is for the bigger stuff, you get a blade part, a pencil part, and the center spike. As you can see you just move it to where you want it and do your thing. The attachments are from micromark...I can give you the catalogue number if you're interested. I think they're designed to fit a wooden ruler thats thicker than the metal one, so I had to put bit of styrene packing in to tighten them up, but no big problem really. The ruler's easy to find from hardware or DIY places.

[IMAGE: lrgcuttersml.jpg]

Cheers

Phil

Post #126  (forum post #1003630)
Author    : Clerval
Date      : Oct 6, 2009 at 8:00 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ even more newer pics page 12

The circle cutter's can take care of some fairly thick styrene... like cutting anything else, you just have to be sure to lightly score it at first, and go 'round a few times. You'll be able to bend and snap it pretty quickly, just be careful not to do it too soon, or you can end up with a slight angled edge.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more newer pics page 7

Lee, I dunno if you've seen it but evergreen do a sheet of "clapboard" that has a similar ribbing to the zip tie. I thought I'd mention it 'cos the sheet's quite thin, about .75mm...I thought it might be easier to bend and cut if you need something to wrap around a smaller dia..

Also those tie's are from poundworld or poundland..can't remember the difference, anyhoo, they had a couple of different sizes and there's quite a few in the packet so if you want a few LMK. 

Bests

Phil

the M60A1 has some parts such as the vents on the bottom / rear of the falcon but it does not have these as shown on the sidewall photo.

Better off just getting the M60A2 & you should be in good shape (its on the more expensive side of 1/35 Tamiya kits)

The red arrow part is something underneath the marder part with the cross on it...dunno what it is though.

This thing is driving me nuts !!, I just wannna finish the darn thing:cry

Also, the rear edge with the spoilers, boxy bits with the little rivet detail, and connecting rods still has me stumped...castings of any...especially the boxes would be fab !!

Anybody got landing gear ?

Cheers

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more newer pics page 7

Ok guys here goes, another update..usual stuff, bit of this and that, real, cast and scratch. 

These pics are the waist as you can see. I think these are more or less finished. Under paint I'm sure they'll look not too bad.

[IMAGE: acroppedsml.jpg]

[IMAGE: bcroppedsml.jpg]

[IMAGE: ccroppedsml.jpg]

Hmmm..engine deck. This is a bit awkward to get the parts in the right place. A bit of jiggery pokery needed with it. Turns out, the deck plate is about 5-6mm too big/long. I dunno how this has come about, obviously a balls up with my measuring, but it's too late to change it now. Anyway, I've made the Flakvierling suspension bits a little longer to take up a bit of the discrepancy, and the styrene plate underneath is a bit bigger than it needs to be too. It's more than a bit annoying, but there it is...warts and all.:angry If I were to have a go at changing it now, I'd have to rip off the plate which would destroy most of the rear section. Hopefully when it's all nailed down it'll look ok..

[IMAGE: decksml.jpg]

Let me know watcha think, and thanks again as usual to all who have helped me out with ID's and spare parts.
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
thumbsup

Cheers guys

Phil

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 9

Hey guys, more progress on the engine deck..

[IMAGE: decksml.jpg]

[IMAGE: deck1sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: deck2sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: deck5sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: deck4sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: deck3sml.jpg]

It's about done now, I need to make the spoilers next, and do the rods and boxes, but it's getting closer...:wacko

Those elusive wheels...I made them with a sanded down cast of the hanomag wheel and some cut down tubing, I cut some out of the tube to make it smaller and wrapped it around the Hano part, fired superglue at it and the finished one's are on the right. I can't take the credit for the ID of the hanomag part though, Mensaboy over on resin illum did the ID-ing for that bit. Thanks a lot to him !!:cool

[IMAGE: wheelssml.jpg]

Anyway that's it for a bit, won't be much progress now until the new year. Lots of Christmas stuff to do, and the spare room is full of stuff we've moved out of the way to make room for the tree..

Cheers

Phil

Click to expand...

 

Hey Phil,

Dont get me wrong the MR team did an awesome job and ID'ed a ton of parts for this model, but unfortunatly on the final model it looks like every parts was scratched (or 3D printed). Some parts were better reproduced than other but you can definitely say that the parts are not original when you put actual kit parts next to the MR Falcon.

The details of those fins are not really well done (but they reproduced the resin bubbles which were on some of the holes of the DFV parts on the original model ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
), we found the small part next to the extinguisher (the kit, which is used in several place on the Falcon was obviously not found by the MR team), I won't say the name of the kit as I did not found it myself, it's up to the guy who found it if he wants ! I dont have this kit yet myself. 

There's indeed a jack on the opposite side. 

There are indeed a 2 rivets on the L strip, I'm not sure what part it is right now, but it sure looks like some structural parts 'maybe I would need to take a better at the Leopold or Karl). On the MR part, there's also a rivet on the middle of this L-strip, I cant find any evidence of it on my ref pics.

Keep up the good work Phil, you're making an awesome Falcon !

Welcome Mensaboy, and thanks for the engine deck map ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Post #255  (forum post #1531836)
Author    : moes1
Date      : Jan 27, 2011 at 2:09 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 10

Let me put it this way, the majority of parts were delivered to MR, but due to shrinkage the parts seems smaller or more blurry. They were not 3D printed. We also provided MR with casts parts or with the kit info needed if for some reason we did not have the parts. Then a new kit could be bought.

It's correct that some parts were not IDed when we were contracted therefore they had to be scratched. Some I found a few month later, (part mentioned below) after the project were finished unfortunately, but we had a deadline. There are actually still lots of parts yet to be IDed.

MonsieurTox said:

			Hey Phil,

- unfortunatly on the final model it looks like every parts was scratched (or 3D printed). Some parts were better reproduced than other but you can definitely say that the parts are not original when you put actual kit parts next to the MR Falcon.

Post #299  (forum post #1651303)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 12

Thanks guy's, you're all very kind..

Hey Ozzy, the cockpit tube is 3 inches dia, and the door into the cockpit is 1.5 inches high.

I've measured a 1/48th figure and it is 1.5" high, so I reckon the 32" is about 1/48th scale.

I would very much like to see your figures, if you have a pic..

Hey Scratchy, the gun barrels are Moe's castings, I've had them for quite a while, I'm sorry I have no idea what kits, if any were used to make them. You could give Moe a shout....

The heatsink part of the gun is from the AMT X Wing, Julien mentioned this on another forum, so thanks yet again to him ! 

I have the radar to build, this is a Moe cast too, and I also need to add a couple of surface details. The interior of the rear section of the cockpit needs to be scratched,..and the gun mounts need building, and I think that's it...I'm kinda tempted to fire some primer at it before I do the cockpit bit...

Cheers all

Phil

Post #301  (forum post #1652112)
Author    : ozzyguanche
Date      : Apr 25, 2011 at 8:20 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 12

Hi tk1608,

If the tube is 3" then I would suggest the figures are 1.32. I am not sure how you are doing your cockpit (PM sent) but if it is to represent the film set and not the 32" model, then your door is way to small.

Here is a pic of the set design with scale.

[IMAGE: PDVD_016.jpg]

This pic should show up on a 17inch screen as 3", and you can see by the doorway the figure should be about 54mm or around 2" (1/32nd scale).

[IMAGE: BAckPanelBit.jpg]

Hope this is helpfull and not being nitpicking.

Found pics of the figures I did, but not the actual figures. So no use showing if I have not found.

Ozzy

Not weird at all mate, was talking with Lee last night about it, it seems a shame to have all the hard work hidden by paint but at the same time what a thing to paint eh! I still wont re paint my MR till I believe I can do a better job, so to paint a scratch must be so hard.

Still an amazing achievement but the "HOLE WORLD IS WATCHING" well we are!!  So get your shorts n running shoes mate and rattle that primer can.

As for colour I really think dont take advice, you will get so many conflicting idea's your head will spin, as Frankenstein you get to name your own Monster. I would say ask Gunpowder if you can pay him a visit to have a look in the flesh, that may help?

You'll know if its wrong cos you wont be happy, when you look at it and think, yes, then your doing it right mate.

Guys another small update, 

I've been using Ozzy's brilliant graphics to build the cockpit,.. 

[IMAGE: door1sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: cokpt1sml.jpg]

[IMAGE: door2sml.jpg]

Using the graphics as a pattern I transfered the sizes to styrene and cut them out. I intend to print them out again onto decal paper and stick them onto the panels. I'm hoping that the lights I have at the back of the cockpit will shine though when I make some holes, and the thin spaces between the panels on the back wall, will look like the light strips...anyway we'll see..

I dunno if the diamond flooring is cannon, but I thought there must be some sort of flooring there, so I made that bit up..

That's it for now,

Cheers, Phil

Post #354  (forum post #1707054)
Author    : nightrider
Date      : Jun 4, 2011 at 11:20 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 13

ralphee said:

			Apparently so, but have you ever used them? Its about the most nasty paint ive ever put through my brush, basically brain cancer in a jar, even with my mask, i can taste the crap.

Then, there is the case of getting a decent jar or two in the UK, much of the Floquil range ive paid big money for in the UK, has been congealed cheese in a glass jar :lol.

Id go with a custom Tamiya mix, way safer, easier to mix, and easier to get hold of.

lee
		

Click to expand...

Have to agree with that. I used the floquil paints when I repainted my mr falcon and it is some nasty smelling stuff. What I disliked the most about it though was that it seemed difficult to me to get a nice smooth finish. If the mixture wasn't perfect it would always want to make a rough, sandpaper type finish which didn't work as well for me when going back over it with weathering. The "grime" base color would also get yellow streaks in it in any areas that got rubbed too much, which isn't hard to do when you're working over such a large piece. On the other hand, the tamiya paints have always laid down incredibly smooth, aren't very toxic, and make a very durable finish.

That said, I still think I'd acquire one small bottle of each of the primary colors just to make my own color chart of sorts to match the custom mixes to. Since the floquil colors where what was used for the original, they all have a very unique look and I'd try to stay as close to those as possible if it were me. The base for the filming miniature was straight "grime". MR went with a 50/50 mix to make the finished bird look closer to what was seen on screen. Interestingly enough, most of the shipped birds were all considerably darker than straight grime.:lol

GREAT JOB ON THIS BUILD!!!!:thumbsup

Post #366  (forum post #1751400)
Author    : -... . .- --..
Date      : Jul 4, 2011 at 7:09 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 13

Hey Phil,

I know originally the old Floquil Railroad Colors line was lacquer-based with its industrial strength Diosol thinner intended for the metal railroad car hobbyist, and therefore kind of hot for painting directly on styrene. Just one of the reasons most of these studio miniatures were primered first.

When Testors bought Floquil many years ago however, they changed the whole Railroad Color line to an enamel formula. They're the same colors, only much safer for spraying directly on models, which makes sense from Testor's perspective. 

As for whether or not the current iteration will adhere to an acrylic undercoat, I know it works fine over Mr. Surfacer/Mr. Primer, but have no real experience with Halford's primer, so it probably wouldn't hurt to do a good bit of research and testing before trying that combination on your Falcon.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #371  (forum post #1751543)

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 13

tk1608 said:

			Right so, do I need some "grime", and "boxcar red" or somesuch..?
		

Click to expand...

From my own experience and research, including what was apparently used by the model shop to paint Boba Fett's helmet as well, some good enamel Floquil Railroad colors to have on hand for your ESB Falcon are:

Reefer White

Grime

Boxcar Red

Caboose Red

Reefer Gray

Engine Black

Grimy Black

Depot Buff

Southern Pacific Armour Yellow

Reefer Yellow

Dark Blue

Pullman Green

Tuscan

I have one of each Railroad color in the shop, but this subset will get you most of what you'll need for most ILM miniatures. Base coat for the Falcon was apparently a mixture of Reefer White and Grime, some say 50/50.

Post #377  (forum post #1755696)
Author    : nightrider
Date      : Jul 6, 2011 at 11:59 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 13

It shouldn't be hard to mix a base color from tamiya if you have the genuine article to match it to. Without a sample of grime in front of you though it's just gonna be trying to match this or that particular photograph. The base seems to me to be a bit more forgiving as far as a "perfect" match is concerned since it tends to look so different depending on the lighting. The individual panels though? Gonna be hard to match those as perfectly as the original paints. It always seems to pop when those are used. Just looks "right". I would say for the Falcon the bare minimum I'd want would be grime(to match), rust, reefer gray, boxcar red & I believe the other gray used was "primer". Since you're not using floquil for the base coat, you'll only need one bottle of each just for panels. If you can't get these I'll check my stuff and see if I have extras & if so I'd be happy to post them to you. Half a bottle of each will likely do the whole bird. As for the base color, I believe the studio miniature was actually painted in straight grime but it was decided somewhere along the line on the MR bird to do the 50/50 mix with reefer white to more closely resemble what's seen on screen. Under the bright lighting that the falcon was filmed and photographed under it tends to look considerably lighter.

The "rust" I was referring to that Dave's daughter matched was on his sand crawler. Gotta say she's got a great eye, it's a perfect match. Here's the thread.  http://www.therpf.com/f11/my-r-cooper-sandcrawler-progress-71873/index4.html

reefer grey: 3/4 bottle (dark grey panels)

rust: full bottle

grimy black: 1/2 bottle

yellow: full bottle

These are basically all the primary colors you'd need for the panels and should be more than enough to do the whole bird unless you messed up........a lot. Other than grime I can't think of any other floquil colors that were used on the falcon.

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

Guy's I've been trying to locate the floquil stuff here, and phoned quite a few places with not much luck.

Some say they can get it, but because it has a hazardous solvent in there, it has to be shipped by sea, in it's own sealed container, and delivered to the shop by a carrier that specialises in hazardous chemicals.

Hard to believe I know, and it will take weeks or months to get here on top of all that. Also with all the silly regulations it'll push the price up to £5 or about $8 a jar.

Chris, I'm worried that if you send some to me by air, without all these over the top safeguards, that it might get impounded, and I'll never receive it...

I didn't think getting the right paint would be so difficult...I'm thinking that Tamiya mixing time is the way forward.

If anyone has an idea of what the closest colour match to the floquil grime is, I would very much like to hear your opinions. 

Failing that, I'll try gunpowders mix of deck tan/white and see how it looks.

Just been looking through a few paint pots..Tamiya medium grey is a warmish grey that might look ok with some white added, or humbrol 129 light gull grey...this looks pretty close to my MR snowspeeder colour....hmmmm

Dunno what else to add..I'm a bit frustated....

Cheers

Phil

Post #408  (forum post #1823338)
Author    : tk1608

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

So Blokes and Blokettes, another small update...you saw the grey primer pics earlier, so after that I did this...

[IMAGE: bellypreshadesml.jpg]

However..this was a big mistake,, because, I got hold of some of the floquil paint after I did this preshade, and it turns out the floquil is very thin and can be airbrushed straight from the bottle. So even though the grey primer doesn't look very dark on the pic,.. it's darker in real life btw, ...it was a pig to cover, and I used half a jar just to cover the smaller parts of the model. I didn't even start to do the main ship. I realised that I wouldn't have enough to do the whole thing with the one and a half jars I had left...what a balls up !

So, Back to the garage, and out with the white primer, and this was the result..

[IMAGE: toprepaintwhitesml.jpg]

It ended up being a very light grey in fact, but much easier to cover with the main colour now..

After that I mixed up some tamiya paint to match as close as I could to the floquil grime. I fired this mix at everything so hopefully the grime will go on over it easily, and I'll have the real base colour on there to start the next stage..

pic below has just the tamiya mix and a bit of weathered black in the pits and the engine vents..no grime on it yet..

[IMAGE: toptamiya1stcoatsml.jpg]

I was surprised how light a shade the grime is though, I was expecting it to be more of a light gull grey kind of colour, but it's more a very slightly dirty white...if MR lightened it up for their model it seems a bit odd, it's very light already...

Anyhoo, I managed to get all the floquil colours apart from boxcar red and reefer grey...I reckon I can mix the boxcar from the caboose red with a bit of rust added, and I'm sure I can knock up a tamiya mix for the reefer grey. Looooonnng way to go yet though..

Comments, advice, abuse, laughter, always welcome..:lol

Cheers

Phil

Post #417  (forum post #1829724)
Author    : nightrider
Date      : Aug 19, 2011 at 8:52 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

Lookin good man! Glad to see you're into the painting. Honestly, if your Tamiya mix is a good match I would skip the floquil altogether for the base. The floquil won't make as smooth a finish. Another thing, if you do use the grime, don't use the sanding pads! It will turn a light yellowish color wherever it's abraded. Even just lightly scratching it with your fingernail will make a yellowish streak. When I did some painting on my MR falcon I tried sanding a few places to smooth out the finish and it turned it a very light yellow. Don't know if others have had that same experience, but I have every time I've used it. If you use the floquil it would actually be good to put a flat clear over it to prevent abrading the paint when you start to handle it for the rest of the work.

As for the MR bird, they did approve a 50/50 mix of grime and reefer white; however, all the factory ones were considerably darker than straight grime.:lol Pretty much straight up tan. Never figured that one out. 

Chris

Phil mate, just go with your heart, if it bugs you now it will bug you for ever. Think about what will go on top of the panels re weathering etc. Will this change the look to be more how you want. If your not happy start over on them. It doesn't matter if they look the same as the pics as these just dont help. Choose one single ref pic that you think has the colour you want then go for that colour.

Too much info will clog up the results you want to get! Post a pic of the best ref shot you have re colour for the panels and lets see the comparison to your colour?

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

Hi Phil,

I know what you're going through. From my experiences as a graphic designer and illustrator, I've found that no one will ever match a color by going off any image you find in a book or archive. Unless you have the original sitting beside you or an actual paint chip you'll have to "wing it".

I think it looks good, but by the sounds of it you feel it's just "Okay". So if it were me I would change it now before you move forward. It'll be easier to do it now than later (when you have the other colors down). Guy is right... "if it bugs you now it will bug you forever."

From time to time, people think I'm crazy for starting over halfway through a project/job... but it has to do with listening to your gut.

Well that's my two cents. You're doing a great job. Just RELAX about the colors and paint... this should be the fun part.:lol

Post #455  (forum post #1877562)
Author    : nightrider
Date      : Sep 9, 2011 at 7:28 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

It can drive you nuts if you're picky like I am. That's why I went with the original colors, so I would no that despite my obsessiveness, they would be as close to right as is possible. Looking at my bird that Dean painted right now & that color does have a blue tone. If you'll notice, the large triangular panel with the large rectangular one below it near the cockpit, both have a slightly washed out appearance. When i redid my MR falcon I used the base coat and very lightly added the washed out area near the center. I don't know if on the original it was just because the panel was lightly painted for that kind of effect or if it's the weathering around it that makes the center look lighter but I tend to think it was just sprayed on very thinly. You'll notice some panels, especially the concrete ones like around the turret, are painted very lightly so that they are transparent and the base coat shows through them. Be careful when you do those panels not to over do it or the color will be to dark. Here is what the panel looked like on mine after I lightened the center a bit.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #471  (forum post #1904558)
Author    : -... . .- --..
Date      : Sep 21, 2011 at 9:18 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

Hey Phil,

She's really coming along beautifully now, you've come a long way already.

As for the straight-line streaking, you can hand brush it with a really thin wash and the straight edge of a piece of paper. Here's a guy who used a combination of paint and pastels to do the same trick on his Fine Molds Falcon:

Building the Falcon: Deconstructing the damage

If you want a really sharp line, you can use the sticky end of a post-it note. As with any technique like this, practice makes perfect.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #489  (forum post #1924972)
Author    : Scott Graham

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

When learning to paint with gouache in my industrial design classes we used to use these architect's rulers to run the brush along in order to make straight lines with paint. It's very easy to do. The triangular section of it ensures only the handle of your brush touches it further up than the bristles. I recommend it for your streaks.

Post #501  (forum post #1935056)
Author    : Scratchy
Date      : Oct 7, 2011 at 2:19 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

tk1608 said:

			Hey Scott & Scratchy do you have a pic of this technique please ?

Thanks guys, 

Phil
		

Click to expand...

Phil,

I have three pics. All the same with the exception of the brushes that I've used and a demo of both rulers.  I don't know if you're right or left handed, but I'm right handed.

Notice how I'm holding the ruler with my left hand,.... four fingers below the ruler and my thumb applying pressure to the ruler, while keeping it firmly against the paper on an angle, raised at the front.

As I keep this locked in position with my left hand and angled and raised on the paper, I have the brush in my right hand, with my hand riding along the ruler, while holding the brush tight, not moving the brush up or down, only in one direction from left to right and with the metal collar of the brush against the edge of the ruler.

I used a #8 Rigger brush and a #3/0 Detail round brush (bottom pic)  Depending how much paint you have on the brush, and how lightly you're gliding along the paper, you could make a very fine line with it.  However, it takes practice.

[IMAGE: brushstrokes.jpg]

I prefer an old fashioned wooden ruler with a metal ink-edge intact.  They last forever, if taken care of.  I had this one since my illustration classes back in '91-'92 and it's still good.

The plastic drafting ruler that I have, has a wonderfull assortment of nicks and dents, which makes for a difficult straight line.

I hope this helps.

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 16

Just want to help with the drafting ruler. The way I used it was to just rest the one of the three edges on the surface so you don't hold the brush at an angle. And the ticks molded into the measurements can be sanded. It's the best method I've ever seen to make straight paint lines when used this way.

Post #557  (forum post #2115714)
Author    : tk1608
Date      : Jan 30, 2012 at 8:44 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: 32" Falcon Progress/ more new piccys page 21

Hey guys, thanks yet again for all the kind words..
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Just a few more pics...all painting is done now..even the dreaded splatter..:love

[IMAGE: IMG_5110.jpg]

[IMAGE: IMG_5109.jpg]

[IMAGE: IMG_5107.jpg]

A quick lighting test...they haven't been on for about 3 years.. they still work..:thumbsup

The engine light isn't as bright as I hoped, but anyhoo..pics..

[IMAGE: IMG_5170.jpg]

[IMAGE: IMG_5167.jpg]

This is to light up the strip lights on the back wall..

[IMAGE: IMG_5169.jpg]

so you get this..you get the idea..

[IMAGE: IMG_5172.jpg]

scratched interior

[IMAGE: IMG_5173.jpg]

Dashboard..

[IMAGE: IMG_5174.jpg]

Ozzy sent me his brilliant graphics, so I printed them out onto decal paper..

[IMAGE: IMG_5175.jpg]

And applied them like this..

[IMAGE: IMG_5178.jpg]

Looks pretty good I reckon..Big thanks to Ozzy..
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
thumbsup

After the decals had dried I dusted a bit of semi flat clear over them. I then made holes in the wall and put fibers in. It's the first time I've ever done this in any model..

[IMAGE: IMG_5180.jpg]

This is it with the light from the window showing where the holes are. 

[IMAGE: IMG_5179.jpg]

I'm gonna add some red white and blue LEDs to it...hopefully I'll be able to fit them in the space behind the round cabinet light you saw earlier..

Very close to total completion...

Cheers guys

Phil

I know this forum is a few years old, but it has inspired me to give this a go.  Beautiful work my friend! Truly inspiring.  I am having trouble figuring out the height of my falcon. May I ask how tall you made your ribs to give me the curve of the hull?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #617  (forum post #2409661)
Author    : tk1608
Date      : Aug 9, 2012 at 4:44 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

My ribs are 35mm at the highest point, and the curve tapers off to nothing. You've got to check this yourself though to see if you agree. I worked it out depending on styrene thickness etc and that's what I came up with. It's all subjective this stuff...

Hope it helps

Cheers 

Phil

thumbsup

[IMAGE: IMG_5180.jpg]

This is it with the light from the window showing where the holes are. 

[IMAGE: IMG_5179.jpg]

I'm gonna add some red white and blue LEDs to it...hopefully I'll be able to fit them in the space behind the round cabinet light you saw earlier..

Very close to total completion...

Phil

Author    : tk1608
Date      : Feb 19, 2013 at 7:21 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi, the circles are rub down decals, and the black lines are done with a ruler and a fine permanent marker with a dusting of the base colour over the top to dull the sheen..

Cheers

Phil

derekcwicks: unfortunately this is the wrong kit. it has the changed parts. you need this version of the Shinano (vintage/old tooling) for the correct parts, which are: 1,2,3,4,11,12,19,29,30,32,33.

[IMAGE: 460528-c01d23bd3eb023d64f8658f4a4a256b5.jpg]
 
[IMAGE: 460529-4d26fc3c19338555c9b87a1096c29ef7.jpg]
 

this kit is indeed very rare and only pops up on ebay from time to time. if you are lucky you can snatch it for a few bucks.
